25:T838,<entryFree id="n12459" key="دِرَاكٌ" type="main">     
                  <form>       
                     <itype>3</itype>        
                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">دِرَاكٌ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">دراك</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">درى</orth>
                  </form> The <hi rend="ital">making one part,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">portion,</hi> of a thing, (K, TA,) whatever it be, (TA,) <hi rend="ital">to follow another uninterruptedly;</hi> (K, TA;) as also <foreign lang="ar">مُدَارَكَةٌ</foreign>: (TA:) both [are inf. ns. of <foreign lang="ar">دارك</foreign>, and] signify the same [i. e. <hi rend="ital">the continuing,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">carrying on,</hi> a thing <hi rend="ital">uninterruptedly</hi>]: (S:) <foreign lang="ar">مُدَارَكَةٌ</foreign> is when there are no intervals between things following one another; like <foreign lang="ar">مُوَاصَلَةٌ</foreign>: otherwise it is <foreign lang="ar">مُوَاتَرَةٌ</foreign>. (S and K in art. <foreign lang="ar">وتر</foreign>.) You say, of a man, <foreign lang="ar">دارك صَوْتَهُ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">He continued his voice uninterruptedly.</hi> (S, TA.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  Also A horse's <hi rend="ital">overtaking,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">coming up with,</hi> wild animals (K, TA) &amp;c. (TA.) You say, of a horse, <foreign lang="ar">دارك الوَحْشَ</foreign>, inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">دِرَاكٌ</foreign>, <hi rend="ital">He overtook,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">come up with, the wild animals.</hi> (TK.) [Thus it is syn. with <foreign lang="ar">ادرك</foreign>.]          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  In the saying, <foreign lang="ar">لَا بَارَكَ ٱللّٰهُ فِيهِ وَلَا دَارَكَ</foreign>, (S, K, * TA,) it is an imitative sequent: (K, TA:) all these verbs have one and the same meaning. (S, TA. [See <foreign lang="ar">تَارَكَ</foreign>.])    </entryFree>26:T255b,<entryFree id="n12460" key="ادركهُ" type="main">     
                  <form>       
                     <itype>4</itype>        
                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">ادركهُ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">أدرك</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">أدركه</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ادركه</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ادركة</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">درك</orth>
                  </form>, (S Msb, K, &amp;c.,) inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">إِدْرَاكٌ</foreign> (S, Msb) and <foreign lang="ar">مُدْرَكٌ</foreign>, (Msb,) <hi rend="ital">He,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">it, attained, reached, overtook,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">came up with, him,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">it:</hi> (S, K, TA:) or <hi rend="ital">sought,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">pursued, and attained, reached,</hi> &amp;c., <hi rend="ital">him,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">it:</hi> (Msb:) [<foreign lang="ar">داركهُ</foreign>, also, signifies the same, as shown above:] and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n12460-1" target="تداركهُ" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>, likewise, [of which <foreign lang="ar">اِدَّراَكَهُ</foreign> is a variation,] is syn. with <foreign lang="ar">ادركهُ</foreign>; (Jel in lxviii. 49, and KL, * and TA; *) and so is   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n12460-2" target="اِدَّرَكَهُ" n="2" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>. (TA.) You say, <foreign lang="ar">أَدْرَكْتُ الرَّجُلَ</foreign> and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n12460-3" target="اِدَّرَكْتُهُ" n="3" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign> [<hi rend="ital">I attained, reached, overtook,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">came up with, the man</hi>]. (IJ, TA.) And <foreign lang="ar">مَشَيْتُ حَتَّى أَدْرَكْتُهُ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">I walked,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">went on foot, until I overtook him,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">came up with him.</hi> (S, TA.) And <foreign lang="ar">عِشْتُ حَتَّى أَدْرَكْتُ زَمَانَهُ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">I lived until I attained,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">reached, his time.</hi> (S, TA.) And <foreign lang="ar">أَدْرَكْتُ الفَائِتَ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">I attained,</hi> &amp;c., <hi rend="ital">that which was passing away</hi>]. (Mgh.) And <foreign lang="ar">ادركهُ بِمَكْرُوهٍ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">He overtook him,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">visited him, with some displeasing,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">abominable,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">evil, action</hi>]. (M and K in art. <foreign lang="ar">وتر</foreign>. See also 6, in the latter half of the paragraph, in two places: and see 10, first sentence.) And <foreign lang="ar">أَدْرَكَنِى الجَهْدُ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">Difficulty,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">distress,</hi> &amp;c., <hi rend="ital">overtook me, ensued to me,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">came upon me</hi>]; a phrase similar to <foreign lang="ar">بَلَغَنِى</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">الكِبَرُ</foreign> in the Kur [iii. 35]: and so <foreign lang="ar">أَدْرَكْتُ الجَهْدَ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">I came to experience difficulty,</hi> &amp;c.]; like <foreign lang="ar">بَلَغْتُ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">مِنَ الكِبَرِ عُتِيًا</foreign> in the Kur [xix. 9]. (Er-Rághib, TA in art. <foreign lang="ar">بلغ</foreign>.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  [Hence, <hi rend="ital">He attained, obtained,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">acquired, it;</hi> and so   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n12460-4" target="تداركهُ" n="4" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>, as is shown in the KL; so too <foreign lang="ar">ادرك بِهِ</foreign>, for one says,] <foreign lang="ar">ادرك بِدَمِهِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">He obtained revenge,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">retaliation, for his blood</hi>]. (S in art. <foreign lang="ar">وتر</foreign>.)          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  [Hence also, <hi rend="ital">He perceived it; attained a knowledge of it by any of the senses.</hi>] You say, <foreign lang="ar">أَدْرَكْتُهُ بِبَصَرِى</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">I perceived it by my sight;</hi>] <hi rend="ital">I saw it.</hi> (S, TA.) <foreign lang="ar">لَا تُدْرِكُهُ الأَبْصَارُ</foreign>, in the Kur [vi. 103], means, accord. to some, <hi rend="ital">The eyes</hi> [<hi rend="ital">perceive him not</hi>]: accord. to others, <hi rend="ital">the mental perception comprehendeth not</hi> [or <hi rend="ital">attaineth not the knowledge of</hi>] <hi rend="ital">the real nature of his hallowed essence.</hi> (TA.) You say also, <foreign lang="ar">ادرك عِلْمِى</foreign>, meaning <hi rend="ital">My knowledge comprehended</hi> that such a thing was a fact. (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="4">-b4-</sense>  [Hence likewise, as an intrans. v., or a trans. v. of which the objective complement is understood,] <foreign lang="ar">ادرك</foreign> also signifies [<hi rend="ital">He attained a knowledge of the uttermost of a thing;</hi> or] <hi rend="ital">his knowledge attained the uttermost of a thing.</hi> (TA.) See also 6, in the former half of the paragraph, in two places.          <sense type="b" n="5">-b5-</sense>  Also <hi rend="ital">It</hi> (a thing) <hi rend="ital">attained its proper time:</hi> (Msb, K:) <hi rend="ital">it attained its final time</hi> or <hi rend="ital">state,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">its utmost point</hi> or <hi rend="ital">degree.</hi> (K.) [<hi rend="ital">He</hi> (a boy, and a beast,) <hi rend="ital">attained his perfect, ripe,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">mature, state;</hi> and in like manner <foreign lang="ar">ادركت</foreign> is said of a girl: or it is like <foreign lang="ar">ادرك</foreign> as meaning] <hi rend="ital">he</hi> (a boy) <hi rend="ital">attained to puberty,</hi> (S, Msb,) or <hi rend="ital">to the utmost term of youth.</hi> (TA.) <hi rend="ital">It</hi> (fruit) <hi rend="ital">attained to ripeness,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">maturity; became ripe,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">mature;</hi> (S Msb;) <hi rend="ital">attained its time, and its utmost degree of ripeness</hi> or <hi rend="ital">maturity.</hi> (T, TA.) And <foreign lang="ar">ادركت القِدْرُ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">The cooking-pot attained its proper time</hi> [<hi rend="ital">for the cooking of its contents</hi>]. (TA.) And <foreign lang="ar">ادركت الخَمْرُ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">The wine became mature</hi>]. (Msb and K in art. <foreign lang="ar">خمر</foreign>.) And <foreign lang="ar">ادرك مَآءُ الرَّكِيَّةِ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">The water of the well reached its</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">دَرَك</foreign>, i. e. its <hi rend="ital">bottom</hi> (Aboo-' Adnán, TA.)          <sense type="b" n="6">-b6-</sense>  Also <hi rend="ital">It passed away and came to an end; came to nought; became exhausted;</hi> or <hi rend="ital">failed entirely:</hi> (S, K:) said in this sense of flour, or meal: (S:) and thus it has been explained as used in the Kur [xxvii. 68], where it is said, [accord. to one reading,] <foreign lang="ar">بَلْ أَدْرَكَ عِلْمُهُمْ فِى الآخِرَةِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">Nay, their knowledge hath entirely failed respecting the world to come</hi>]. (TA. [See also 6.]) Sh mentions this signification as heard by him on no other authority than that of Lth; and Az asserts it to be incorrect: but it has been authorized by more than one of the leading lexicologists, and the language of the Arabs does not forbid it; for it is said of flour, or meal, and in this case can only mean <hi rend="ital">it came to its end, and entirely failed,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">became exhausted;</hi> and fruits, when they are ripe (<foreign lang="ar">إِذَا أَدْرَكْتْ</foreign>) are exposed to coming to nought, and so is everything that has attained to its extreme term; so that the signification of “ coming to nought ” is one of the necessary adjuncts of the meaning of <foreign lang="ar">إِدْرَاكٌ</foreign>. (TA.) [In like manner,]   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n12460-5" target="اِدَّرَكَ" n="5" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n12462"/></foreign> signifies <hi rend="ital">It</hi> (a thing) <hi rend="ital">continued uninterruptedly and then come to nought:</hi> (IJ, TA:) and agreeably with this signification is explained the saying in the Kur [xxvi. 61], <foreign lang="ar">إِنَّا لَمُدَّرِكُونَ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">Verily we are coming to nought,</hi> by those who read thus instead of <foreign lang="ar">لَمُدْرَكُونَ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">being overtaken</hi>]. (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="7">-b7-</sense>  You say also, <foreign lang="ar">ادرك الثَّمَنُ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">المُشْتَرِىَ</foreign>, meaning [The payment of] <hi rend="ital">the price was,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">became, obligatory on the purchaser:</hi> this is an ideal reaching, or overtaking. (Msb.)    </entryFree>27:T270a,<entryFree id="n12461" key="تدّاركوا" type="main">

                  <hi rend="ital">i. q.</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">تلاحقوا</foreign> (S) [i. e.] <hi rend="ital">They attained, reached, overtook,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">came up with, one another;</hi> as also <foreign lang="ar">اِدَّارَكُوا</foreign>, and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n12461-1" target="اِدَّرَكُوا" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>; (Sh, TA;) [or] <hi rend="ital">the last of them attained, reached, overtook,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">came up with, the first of them.</hi> (S Msb, K, TA.) Hence, in the Kur [vii. 36], (S,) <foreign lang="ar">حَتَّى إِذَا ٱدَّارَكُوا فِيهَا جَمِيعًا</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">Until, when they have overtaken one another,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">have successively arrived, therein, all together</hi>]: originally <foreign lang="ar">تَدَارَكُوا</foreign>. (S, K. *) And <foreign lang="ar">تدارك الثَّرِيَانَ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">The two moistures reached each other;</hi> (like <foreign lang="ar">اِلْتَقَى الثَّرَيَانِ</foreign>;) meaning] <hi rend="ital">the moisture of the rain reached the moisture of the earth.</hi> (S.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  And [hence] <foreign lang="ar">تدارك</foreign> signifies [<hi rend="ital">It continued,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">was carried on, uninterruptedly; it was closely consecutive in its parts,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">portions;</hi>] <hi rend="ital">one part,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">portion, of it, followed,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">was made to follow, another uninterruptedly;</hi> said of anything. (TA.) You say, <foreign lang="ar">تدارك السَّيْرُ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">The course,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">pace,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">journeying, continued uninterruptedly</hi>]. (S and TA in art. <foreign lang="ar">حفد</foreign>, &amp;c.) And <foreign lang="ar">تداركت الأَخْبَارُ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">The tidings followed one another closely.</hi> (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  [Hence, when said of knowledge, meaning, accord. to Fr, <hi rend="ital">It continued unbroken in its sequence</hi> or <hi rend="ital">concatenation.</hi>] <foreign lang="ar">بَلِ ٱدَّرَاكَ عِلْمُهُمْ فِى الآخِرَةِ</foreign> (K, TA,) in the Kur [xxvii. 68], (TA,) [virtually] means <hi rend="ital">Nay, they have no knowledge respecting the world to come:</hi> (K, TA:) or, as IJ says, <hi rend="ital">their knowledge is hasty, and slight, and not on a sure footing,</hi> &amp;c.: Az says that AA read <foreign lang="ar">بَلْ أَدْرَكَ</foreign> [of which an explanation has been given above (see 4)]: that I'Ab is related to have read   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n12461-2" target="بَلَىآأَدْرَكَ" n="2" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign> [&amp;c., i. e. <hi rend="ital">Yea, hath their knowledge reached its end</hi> &amp;c.?], as interrogatory, and without tesh-deed: and that, accord. to the reading <foreign lang="ar">بل ادّراك</foreign> Fr says that the proper meaning is, [<hi rend="ital">Nay,</hi>] <hi rend="ital">hath their knowledge continued unbroken so as to extend to the knowledge of the world to come,</hi> whether it will be or not be? wherefore is added, <foreign lang="ar">بَلْ هُمْ فِى شَكٍّ مِنْهَا بَلْ هُمْ مِنْهَا عَمُونَ</foreign>: he says also that Ubeí read, <foreign lang="ar">أَمْ تَدَارَكَ</foreign>; and that the Arabs substitute <foreign lang="ar">بَلْ</foreign> for <foreign lang="ar">أَمْ</foreign>, and <foreign lang="ar">أَمْ</foreign> for <foreign lang="ar">بَلْ</foreign>, when a passage begins with an interrogation: but this explanation of Fr is not clear; the meaning is [said to be] <hi rend="ital">their knowledge shall be unbroken and concurrent</hi> [<hi rend="ital">respecting the world to come</hi>] when the resurrection shall have become a manifest event, and they shall have found themselves <pb n="874"/> to be losers; and the truth of that wherewith they have been threatened shall appear to them when their knowledge thereof will not profit them: accord. to Aboo-Mo'ádh the Grammarian, the readings   
      <foreign lang="ar">بَلْ <ref cref="n12461-3" target="أَدْرَكَ" n="3" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign> &amp;c. and <foreign lang="ar">بَلِ ٱدَّارَكَ</foreign> &amp;c. mean the same; i. e. <hi rend="ital">they shall know in the world to come;</hi> like the saying in the Kur [xix. 39], <foreign lang="ar">أَسْمِعْ بِهِمْ وَأَبْصِرْ</foreign>, &amp;c.: and Es-Suddee says of both these readings that the meaning is, <hi rend="ital">their knowledge shall agree,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">be in unison, in the world to come;</hi> i. e. they shall know in the world to come that that wherewith they have been threatened is true: or, accord. to Mujáhid, the meaning of <foreign lang="ar">بَلِ ٱدَّارَكَ عِلْمُهُمْ</foreign> &amp;c. is said to be, <hi rend="ital">is their knowledge concurrent respecting the world to come?</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">بل</foreign> being here used in the sense of <foreign lang="ar">أَم</foreign>: (TA:) or it may mean <hi rend="ital">their knowledge hath gone on uninterruptedly until it hath become cut short;</hi> from the phrase <foreign lang="ar">تدارك بَنُو فُلَانٍ</foreign> meaning <hi rend="ital">The sons of such a one went on uninterruptedly into destruction.</hi> (Bd.)       <sense type="A" n="2">-A2-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">تداركهُ</foreign>: see 4, in two places.                   <foreign lang="ar">نِعْمَةٌ مِنْ رَبِّهِ لَنُبِذَ بِٱلْعَرَآءِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">Had not favour</hi> (<hi rend="ital">meaning mercy,</hi> Jel) <hi rend="ital">from his Lord reached him,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">overtaken him, he had certainly been cast upon the bare land</hi>]. (Jel.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  [Hence, elliptically, <hi rend="ital">He overtook him,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">visited him, with good,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">with evil.</hi>] El-Mutanebbee says, <quote>

                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">دَرَكٌ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">در</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">درك</orth>
                  </form> The act of <hi rend="ital">attaining, reaching,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">overtaking;</hi> syn. <foreign lang="ar">لَحَاقٌ</foreign>; (K, TA; [in the CK, <foreign lang="ar">اللِّحاقُ</foreign> is erroneously put for <foreign lang="ar">اللَّحَاقُ</foreign>;]) [properly an inf. n. of the unused verb <foreign lang="ar">دَرَكَ</foreign> (q. v.), but, having no used verb, said to be] a noun from <foreign lang="ar">الإِدْرَاكُ</foreign> [with which it is syn.], (TA,) or a noun from <foreign lang="ar">أَدْرَكْتُ الشَّىْءَ</foreign>; as also   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n12465-1" target="دَرْكٌ" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n12464"/></foreign>: and hence <foreign lang="ar">ضَمَانٌ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">الدَّرَكِ</foreign> [which see in what follows]. (Msb.) [Hence,] <foreign lang="ar">لَا تَخَافُ دَرَكًا</foreign>, in the Kur [xx. 80.], means <hi rend="ital">Thou shalt not fear</hi> Pharaoh's <hi rend="ital">overtaking</hi> thee. (TA.) One says also <foreign lang="ar">فَرَسٌ <ref cref="n12465-2" target="دَرْكُ" n="2" type="5" subtype="FSO" lang="ar"/>الطَّريدَةِ</foreign>, meaning <hi rend="ital">A horse that overtakes what is hunted;</hi> like as they said <foreign lang="ar">فَرَسٌ قَيْدُ الأَوَابِدِ</foreign>. (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>           <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  Also The <hi rend="ital">attainment,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">acquisition, of an object of want:</hi> and the <hi rend="ital">seeking the attainment</hi> or <hi rend="ital">acquisition thereof:</hi> as in the saying, <foreign lang="ar">بَكِّرْ فَفِيهِ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">دَرَكٌ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">Be thou early; for therein is attainment,</hi> &amp;c.]: and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n12465-3" target="دَرْكٌ" n="3" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n12464"/></foreign> signifies the same. (Lth, TA.) [Hence, perhaps,] <foreign lang="ar">يَوْمُ الدَّرِكَ</foreign>: this was [a day of contest] between El-Ows and El-Khazraj: (K:) thought to be so by IDrd. (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="4">-b4-</sense>  And <hi rend="ital">i. q.</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">تَبِعَةٌ</foreign> [i. e. <hi rend="ital">A consequence;</hi> generally meaning <hi rend="ital">an evil consequence:</hi> and perhaps it also means here <hi rend="ital">a claim which one seeks to obtain for an injury</hi>]: as also   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n12465-4" target="دَرْكٌ" n="4" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n12464"/></foreign>. (S, K.) One says, <foreign lang="ar">مَا لَحِقَكَ مِنْ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">دَرَكٍ فَعَلَىِّ خَلَاصُهُ</foreign> (S, TA) and   
      <foreign lang="ar">من <ref cref="n12465-5" target="دَرْكٍ" n="5" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign> [i. e. <hi rend="ital">Whatever evil consequence ensue to thee, on me be the compensation thereof</hi>]: in the A, <foreign lang="ar">ما أَدْرَكَهُ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">من دَرَكٍ فعلىّ خلاصه</foreign> i. e. <foreign lang="ar">مَا يَلْحَقُهُ مِنْ تَبِعَةٍ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">Whatever evil consequence ensue to it,</hi> &amp;c.; relating to a thing sold]. (TA.) And hence <foreign lang="ar">ضَمَانُ الدَّرَكِ</foreign> in the case of a claim for indemnification for a fault of a defect or an imperfection in a thing sold [meaning either <hi rend="ital">Responsibility,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">indemnification,</hi> (see <foreign lang="ar">ضَمَانٌ</foreign>,) <hi rend="ital">for evil consequence</hi>]: (TA in the present art:) or this means [<hi rend="ital">indemnification for evil consequence in a sale;</hi> i. e., virtually,] <hi rend="ital">the returning of the price to the purchaser on the occasion of requirement by the thing sold:</hi> the vulgar say incorrectly [<foreign lang="ar">ضَمَان دَرَك</foreign>, and still more incorrectly] <foreign lang="ar">ضُمَان دَرَك</foreign> [generally meaning thereby I sell this, or I purchase this, on the condition of <hi rend="ital">responsibility,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">indemnification, for any fault</hi> or <hi rend="ital">defect</hi> or <hi rend="ital">imperfection</hi> that may be found in it]: (TA in art. <foreign lang="ar">ضمن</foreign>:) [and in this manner <foreign lang="ar">ضَمَانُ الدَّرَكِ</foreign> may be correctly rendered; for] <foreign lang="ar">دَرَكٌ</foreign> also signifies <hi rend="ital">a fault</hi> or <hi rend="ital">a defect</hi> or <hi rend="ital">an imperfection</hi> [in a thing sold]; for instance, in a slave that is sold. (TA in art. <foreign lang="ar">عهد</foreign>.) [In the KT, <foreign lang="ar">الدَّرَكُ</foreign> is also explained as signifying <hi rend="ital">The purchaser's taking from the seller a pledge for the price that he has given him, in fear that the thing sold may require it:</hi> but this seems to be an explanation of the case in which the word is used; not of the word itself.]       <sense type="A" n="2">-A2-</sense>  Also <hi rend="ital">A rope,</hi> (M, K,) or <hi rend="ital">a piece of rope,</hi> (S,) <hi rend="ital">that is tied upon the</hi> [<hi rend="ital">lower</hi>] <hi rend="ital">extremity of the main rope</hi> (S, M, K) <hi rend="ital">of a well, to the cross pieces of wood of the bucket,</hi> (S,) <hi rend="ital">so as to be that which is next the water,</hi> (S, M, K,) <hi rend="ital">in order that the main rope may not rot</hi> (S, M) <hi rend="ital">in the drawing of water:</hi> (M:) or <hi rend="ital">a doubled rope that is tied to the cross pieces of wood of the bucket, and then to the main wellrope:</hi> (Az, TA:) and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n12465-6" target="دَرْكٌ" n="6" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n12464"/></foreign> signifies the same. (K. [But only <foreign lang="ar">دَرَكٌ</foreign> is authorized by the TA in this sense.]) [See also <foreign lang="ar">كَرَبٌ</foreign>.]          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  Also, and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n12465-7" target="دَرْكٌ" n="7" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n12464"/></foreign>, The <hi rend="ital">bottom,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">lowest depth,</hi> (Sh, T, S, M, K,) of a thing, (T, M, K,) as of the sea and the like, (T,) or of anything deep, as a well and the like: (Sh:) pl. <foreign lang="ar">أَدْرَاكٌ</foreign>, (K,) a pl. of both, of a form frequent and analogous with respect to the former, but extr. with respect to the latter; and <foreign lang="ar">دَرَكَاتٌ</foreign> also.
